  2598. # [23:16] <dholbert> bsmedberg, coding-style question (feel free to ignore/punt if you're busy): given a pointer "Foo* foo;", do you have any strong feelings on whether it should be null-checked as "if (foo)" vs. "if (!!foo)" ?
  2599. # [23:17] * jlund|lunch is now known as jlund
  2600. # [23:17] <dholbert> bsmedberg, The coding-style guide says to use "if (myPtr)" over "if (myPtr != nullptr)", but it doesn't mention !!myPtr at all
  2601. # [23:19] <nalexander> dholbert: that !! thing is very JavaScript-centric.
  2602. # [23:19] * jlund is now known as jlund|buildduty
  2603. # [23:19] <nalexander> dholbert: because if (foo) does weird things in JS.
  2604. # [23:19] * Quits: florent (Thunderbird@moz-sinhj1.abo.wanadoo.fr) (Connection closed)
  2605. # [23:19] * coop|buildduty is now known as coop
  2606. # [23:19] <nalexander> dholbert: but if (foo) does clear(er) things in C++.
  2607. # [23:19] <dholbert> nalexander, it's an idiom in C++ as well, but not common in moz code AFAIK
  2608. # [23:19] <nalexander> dholbert: sounds like you know more than me.
  2609. # [23:20] <dholbert> nalexander, heh. :) IIUC, the only benefit of using "!!myPtr" as a boolean expression (instead of "myPtr") is that !!myPtr actually compares as equal to true
  2610. # [23:20] <dholbert> (in C++)
  2611. # [23:21] * whimboo is now known as whimboo|afk
  2612. # [23:21] <dholbert> but I'm not sure that matters, because no one should be comparing this for equality to true (in an "if" statement at least)
  2613. # [23:21] <seth> dholbert: i always thought that was a leftover from C, where pre-C99 you had no real bool type
  2614. # [23:21] <seth> dholbert: IMO it is an antipattern in C++
  2615. # [23:22] <seth> (or modern C for that matter, where you should just use bool)
  2616. # [23:22] <dholbert> I can imagine it being useful if you had "bool mEnabled", and you were checking whether mEnabled == somePtr
  2617. # [23:22] <dholbert> then I'd think you'd need to use !! to downconvert somePtr, instead of implicitly upconverting mEnabled
  2618. # [23:23] <seth> dholbert: in C++, in those situations, if (mEnabled == bool(somePtr)) is in my opinion much clearer
